Yesterday's Extraordinary General Meeting of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce 122

Resolved to issue six urgent telegrams

The main purpose is to work together to suppress bandits

And jointly maintain peace and unification The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce held an extraordinary general meeting of members in the conference hall at 2 p.m. yesterday. More than 200 representatives from various industries discussed how to express their opinions on the current situation. It was resolved to issue six urgent telegrams with the main purpose of maintaining peace and unification and working together to suppress bandits. The details of the meeting and the telegrams sent are as follows:

Meeting Staff: Presidium: Wang Xiaolai, Wang

Yansong, Xu Ji, Yuan Ludeng. Recorder: Zhou Songxun. Secretary:

Sun Mingqi, Xue Guangqian, Zhang Bofang, Jin Shengbai, Zhang Yukun, Luo Shiying, Ren Shoupeng.

Meeting Agenda: (1) Jiang (ringing the bell) to start the meeting; (2) All stand at attention; (3) Pay the highest respect to the Party and National Flag and the portrait of the Premier; (4) The Chairman respectfully reads the Premier's will; (5) Silent mourning; (6) Discuss the case of how the Chamber of Commerce should express its opinion on the current situation; (7) Adjourn the meeting.

Discussion Process: After the meeting started, Chairman Wang Xiaolai reported on the purpose of the meeting, saying that this representative conference was convened because of the current situation. The Standing Committee proposed and the Executive Committee decided to convene an extraordinary general meeting of members to discuss, in order to express the opinions of the merchants and people of this city. A total of eight proposals have been received from the representatives, and each of them will be reported first as the basis for discussion, and then the representatives present are invited to express their opinions and discuss solutions together. Then Wang Yansong expressed his

views, briefly saying that since the establishment of the National Government, various political and livelihood aspects at home and abroad have been actively implemented and have achieved considerable results. Now that the Guangdong incident has occurred, its foreign influence prevents the immediate abolition of unequal treaties, giving foreigners an excuse, and the internal obstruction of bandit suppression prevents the central army from concentrating its forces to suppress the communists. At this critical moment of survival, the people should have their say, the main points of which should be: (1) Hoping that the Guangdong side will not make the overall situation糜爛 because of the problem of one or two people; (2) Hoping that party disputes should be resolved legally within the party. In short, today's discussion should be confined to maintaining peace and unification, and the country's expectations should not go beyond this. Then the representatives present successively expressed their opinions: (1) Wu Yunzhai said that the Chamber of Commerce should uphold justice and fairness and issue a declaration so that the Guangdong side can幡然覺悟 and not give the communists an opportunity to cause diplomatic stagnation; otherwise, the people will suffer and both industry and commerce will fall into desperation. (2) Luo Qinghua said that the Chamber of Commerce should take reaching and maintaining peace and unification as the principle, and as for how to express it in order to achieve it, it can be discussed based on the proposal. (3) Chen Liangyu said that a telegram should be sent to the chambers of commerce of various provinces and cities to jointly advocate the formation of a strong and powerful public opinion. (4) Lin Kanghou said that the resolution of the general meeting should take maintaining peace and working together to suppress bandits as the principle, and the methods can be divided into: (A) Sending a telegram to the central government; (B) Persuading Chen Jitang; (C) Sending a telegram to various provinces and cities. In addition, should there be any further expressions, please discuss it. (5) Zhang Meian said that it is possible to speak from the perspective of the merchants and people of the whole city. The first step should be to work together to suppress bandits, which is internal. The second step is to maintain peace and unification, which is external, because only peace and unification can be折衝樽俎. (6) Lu Qisheng said that the people should distinguish right from wrong and blame Chen Jitang for not lightly starting a war and overstepping the norm. (7) Lin Kanghou said that after the resolution of the Chamber of Commerce, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce can send telegrams to the chambers of commerce of various provinces and cities to express their opinions together. In addition, Yang Housheng, Wen Lanting, Cheng Guichu, Huang Fuqing, Qiu Zhidao, Fang Jiren, Chuan Zai, Gao Luxiao, Shao Bao Xing, Xie Zhongle, Xie Fengxiang, Shen Qinglin, Mao Zifang, Zheng Hairuo, Shen Xusheng, Chen Yushu, Luo Hongchan, Wang Jinwen, Hua Chengjin, Yao Run, Zhu Zhenhan, Dong Guitao, Xu Jingzhi, Wang Yunzhang, Xu Chao, Lu Jingwen, Ge Jechen, Xin Wenyao, Yang Shenzhai, Yu Zhiqing, Deng Yunfu, Li Guohua, Wang Hongxiang, Chen Zixiang, Gong Jingyan, Shao Yuerun, Luo Huanzhang, Gu Baoshan, etc. successively put forward proposals. Later, the chairman adopted the opinions of the representatives and expressed and passed the following proposals: (1) Telegraphed the central government to resolve the

Guangdong incident in a political way; (2) Telegraphed Chairman Chiang to support him in going to Jiangxi to supervise the suppression of bandits; (3) Telegraphed Hu Weiyuan Zhantang, requesting him to telegraph the Guangdong side to explain the great righteousness and not overstep the norm; (4) Telegraphed Commander-in-Chief Chen to advise him not to be the initiator of the war; (5) Telegraphed Minister Sun Zhesheng, requesting him to abide by the Premier's will, maintain peace and unification, and handle it properly in coordination with the advanced members of the party; (6) Telegraphed the chambers of commerce of various provinces and cities, requesting them to advocate it unanimously, and resolved that the above six telegrams should be drafted by the standing committee members and jointly recommended by the representatives of the general meeting, Lin Kanghou, Wu Yunzhai, Chen Liangyu, Lao Jingxiu, Wen Lanting, Lu Qisheng, and Luo Qinghua and other seven representatives to sign and review and then issue them after verification. After the meeting, at 5 o'clock, the chairman announced the adjournment of the meeting. After the adjournment, the Standing Committee continued to work with the representatives designated by the General Assembly to draft various telegrams and issued them that night.

Telegram 1: To the Central Party Headquarters of Nanjing, the National Government, the Party Headquarters of various provinces and cities, and the Governments of various provinces: Since the four supervisors of Deng, Lin, and Xiao issued a telegram, the situation has become increasingly serious. Although the advanced members of the party have tried to resolve it by peaceful and appropriate means, the effect has not been significant, and the reaction has been heard from time to time, and the public's psychology has been extremely worried. The above-mentioned military affairs in Henan Province ended last year, and the central government distributed elite troops from the front line in Jiangxi, Hubei, and other provinces to vigorously suppress bandits. It has been half a year since then, and they are still fighting each other in close combat. Not only has there been no time to sweep away the caves and capture the chief, but the bandits' tracks are erratic and they take advantage of loopholes. Even in the areas that have been recovered, they still come back from time to time. Therefore, although the bandit flames seem to be slightly weakening, the people's difficulties have not been greatly eased. What they have been expecting day and night is that the national army's strength is actually superior to the bandits' strength, but it can only be searched for a long time, step by step, and there will eventually be a day when they can be surrounded and annihilated. If the bandit suppression troops are forced to transfer due to the general trend, then the previous events of hungry tigers leaving their cages, Changsha being recaptured last year, and Nanchang being on the verge of danger will not be difficult to repeat. The Yangtze River basin will be permanently reduced to a bandit area, and even the area south of the Five Ridges will not be spared. It is no different

to supply the lives of the Chinese nation to the孤注 of a few people. Moreover, the hidden dangers are more than just this. When Feng and Yan fought each other last year, it was the day of the famine in the Northwest. Traffic was blocked and relief food was cut off, resulting in the starvation of 2 million people in Shaanxi Province alone. Moreover, the elderly and weak were displaced, and their women were mostly贩易 by merchants everywhere. The disaster was unprecedented. Since the end of the anti-rebellion military affairs, although the Northwest relief efforts have been carried out smoothly, if the bandit suppression cannot be ended for a day, the army cannot be demobilized for a day, and the country will not be able to free up a large amount of financial resources to prepare for famine relief. Important External Work is in Progress to Recover the Concessions 123

Notes to various countries will be issued soon

The Sino-Japanese Nanjing Incident has been completely resolved

Foreign Minister Wang talks to reporters yesterday. Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting came to Shanghai to visit his son who was ill in Shanghai. He went to the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 11:00 a.m. yesterday and returned to his residence after working for a while. He took the night train back to Beijing at 11:45 p.m. The reporter of this newspaper met with reporters at the Foreign Office yesterday morning. The reporter first asked if the Sino-Japanese Nanjing Incident had been completely resolved, how much was the compensation amount, and the payment procedures.

Less than one million. Foreign Minister Wang replied that the Sino-Japanese Nanjing Incident had been signed an agreement during the time of Japanese Minister Yoshizawa. This time, he discussed the amount of compensation and payment procedures with Shigemitsu, and it has now been completely resolved. The exact number cannot be remembered, but the compensation for the Nanjing Incident is about 700,000 yuan. The total number of Sino-Japanese Nanjing Incident does not exceed one million yuan. As for the payment procedures, they are paid in ten months, because the Sino-British Nanjing Incident is also paid in more than ten months.

Sino-Soviet Conference Regarding the latest situation of the Sino-Soviet Conference, Wang told reporters that Representative Mo had sent telegrams to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs reporting everything. The eighth meeting was held on June 4, and the ninth meeting was scheduled to be held today (yesterday). The main scope is still discussing the road redemption issue, and the progress is still going smoothly.

Sino-British sovereignty Wang said that negotiations on Sino-British sovereignty in Beijing have been repeatedly negotiated with British Minister Lampson, and considerable results have been discussed. The British Minister took a plane back to Peiping the day before yesterday (6th) and will come south again in autumn to continue negotiations. It is expected that a stage will be reached at that time.

French Concession Case The reporter also asked about the recovery of the French Concession Case. Wang said that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs had negotiated properly with the French Minister on the recovery of the French Concession Council, and it was scheduled to be recovered in mid-July. Therefore, the work of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has come to an end. The Ministry of Justice is now preparing for the handover procedures and various prior arrangements. Regarding the trial of foreign merchants' cases, a special court will be set up. As for the appeal agency, either the Third Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court will be set up or the lawsuit will be directly filed to the Suzhou Higher Court. In addition, all reorganization methods are similar to those of the Special Zone Court.

Recovery of Concessions Wang continued that the recovery of the concessions is the important work of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs this year. It is now preparing to issue notes to the countries concerned, which will be issued in the shortest time. The order of priority for recovery will be determined according to the nature of the concessions. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has a predetermined plan for this, and I am temporarily excused from telling you.

Page 10

Changes in Ambassadors and Consuls The reporter finally asked whether there would be major changes in the overseas ambassadors and consuls as rumored. Foreign Minister Wang said that there would be few changes in the overseas ambassadors and consuls in the future. He also asked about the date of

Envoy Qian Xinzhuan's appointment to France. He replied that Envoy Qian was originally scheduled to leave Shanghai at the end of May, but it may be slightly delayed due to business.

Chinese Merchant Steamships Strike on the Yangtze River 124

Foreign Merchants Implement Monopoly Plan

Guest Gang Gained Petty Advantages

Chinese Shipping Industry Cannot Maintain

The future suffering is still in the hands of the merchant gang. Foreign shipping companies monopolize the shipping industry on the Yangtze River. Chinese shipping companies are seeking countermeasures, and the first step of the foreign merchants' plan has been implemented, which has caused the guest merchants to stop loading Chinese ships, resulting in Chinese merchant ships having to suspend their schedules on the Yangtze River. This matter is of great importance, and the reporter specifically investigated its situation and recorded it as follows:

Rampant price cuts. Cotton yarn is the most important commodity in the river transportation of the Chuan River. Ships from Yichang to Qing Dynasty mostly compete to load this commodity. There are more than 30 foreign ships of British, Japanese, American, and French nationalities on the Yichang to Chongqing route. The water fee for shipping yarn on this route was originally 16 taels per piece, then it fell to 12 taels. Last year, the foreign ships further reduced it and charged 8 taels per piece. According to this number, it is only enough for the shipping cost. This year, foreign merchants are seeking to obtain priority for cargo transportation on the Chuan River and are trying their best to break the Chinese shipping companies' alliance. Therefore, starting from June 1, the water fee for cotton yarn was drastically reduced from 8 taels per piece to 4 taels, and in fact, another tael was given away, and only 3 taels were actually collected. Since this drastic drop in freight rates occurred, foreign ships are prepared to sacrifice and have agreed on three steps. When each Chinese ship follows the price reduction and also charges 4 taels, they will reduce it again and charge 2 taels. The last step is to charge only one tael of water fee per piece of cotton yarn to break the new record of price cuts on the Chuan River and make Chinese ships unable to support themselves.

Tempting the Merchant Gang After the price cuts, foreign ships immediately contacted the guests in Yichang and Chongqing. Those who carry foreign ships will enjoy the preferential benefits of the shortest water fee in the third step. Many short-sighted merchant gangs cannot resist the cheap price and compete to load goods on foreign ships with low freight rates. Those who have signed transportation contracts with Chinese ships also demanded in this price-cutting trend that Chinese ships also reduce their fees according to the freight rates of foreign ships, otherwise they would stop loading.

Fee increase negotiations. If the eight companies such as the Sanyou, Beiyu, Chongqingjiang, China Merchants, Qingping, and Chuanjiang, etc., charge 3 taels less per piece of cotton yarn between Yichang and Chongqing, it is not enough for the coal burning cost, and the wages of the workers and the ship's hardware are completely lost. Such a loss is difficult to maintain. Moreover, if the cargo is in short supply in Sichuan and the price is cut, the loss will be even greater. The Chinese shipping companies put forward negotiations, requesting the merchant gangs to appropriately add to the freight, stating the unavoidable difficulties and further stating that the rampant price cuts of foreign ships are not advisable. Repeated negotiations have yielded no results.

Strike and suspension of traffic. The eight Chinese shipping companies have requested two items from the merchant gangs in Yichang and Chongqing: (1) The water fee should be appropriately increased so that the Chinese ships on the Chuan River can maintain their navigation under the situation of reduced losses, so as to avoid the Jiangshang navigation rights falling entirely into the hands of foreigners, and one day the Chinese merchants will suffer the pain of being slaughtered by them. (2) Maintain the livelihood of the Yichang workers after the Shanghai-Chongqing direct shipping line is opened. The Chinese shipping companies are willing to take care of both sides. In the future, if the Shanghai-Chongqing direct shipping line is operated, two-thirds of the cabin space should be reserved each time to load Yichang goods so that the Yichang small workers can have work and maintain their lives. However, this condition has not been sympathetic to the merchant gangs in Sichuan, and the Sichuan merchants are even more attracted by the price cuts of foreign merchants. Because they did not agree to reduce the fees, they have stopped loading Chinese ships. Yesterday, the various shipping companies in this city received an urgent telegram from Yichang, saying that in the past few weeks, the guest houses have stopped loading Chinese ships, and the Chinese merchant ships on the Chuan River have no business to do. They have to temporarily suspend the traffic and stop the shipping and discuss the rescue plan.

Du Chongyuan's Speech: Go to the Northeast 125

The other day, Mr. Du Chongyuan, manager of the Liaoning Zhaoxin Kiln Industry Company and former representative of the Northeast at the National Assembly, gave a speech at the Shanghai YMCA. The title of his speech was "Go to the Northeast." Mr. Du is currently the chairman of the Liaoning City Chamber of Commerce. He came from a very poor background, and when he grew up, seeing the increasingly aggressive Japanese invasion of the Northeast, he volunteered with the determination to save the country through industry. He went to Japan to study at the Tokyo Higher Industrial School (now Tokyo Institute of Technology), majoring in kiln industry for four years. After completing his studies in the twelfth year of the Republic of China, he returned to China. Initially, he obtained the support of many students who had studied in Japan and jointly invested 6,000 yuan in national currency to organize the Zhaoxin Industrial Company, hoping to save the Northeast provinces from the dumping of Japanese porcelain. After nine years, the achievements

are already quite impressive. The capital has jumped from 6,000 yuan to 500,000 yuan. The factory's manufacturing facilities are all managed using scientific methods, and they are expanding as much as possible within their capacity. Today, the annual production of new-style porcelain bowls reaches 6 million, which is enough to stop the leakage of Japanese goods. Mr. Du is determined to save the country through industry, saying that what the government does not have time to do should be done by the people themselves with the idea of saving the country. He will

go to Hangzhou in the next few days, and then to the ports of Peiping, Tianjin, Harbin, and Jehol to awaken domestic capitalists and ambitious young people to go to the Northeast to develop the natural resources of the Northeast. Mr. Du's intention is actually based on the increasingly aggressive Japanese invasion of the Northeast. If the Chinese people do not save themselves, the resources of the Northeast will fall into the hands of the Japanese. His persuasion in the major ports of the Southeast is aimed at saving the country. The following is an excerpt from Mr. Du's speech at the YMCA on going to the Northeast:

The so-called Northeast refers to the three provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang. Recently, some have included Jehol in the term, but foreigners often refer to the Northeast as Manchuria, or North and South Manchuria. After the Russo-Japanese War, the two powers divided the spoils, and the area south of Changchun along the South Manchurian Railway was called South Manchuria, belonging to Japan. The area north of Changchun along the Chinese Eastern Railway was called North Manchuria, belonging to Russia, to distinguish their spheres of influence. This is the origin of the general term North and South Manchuria, which the Japanese in particular relish, and its intention is the same as the past calling China "Shina," containing the same degree of contempt. They also want to use this to show that the Northeast is not inherent to China and at the same time do not recognize the Northeast as an administrative region of China. Their intentions are extremely dangerous. The Northeast covers an area of 3,506,000 square miles, almost equal to the total area of Germany and France, and three times the size of Japan. The population is only 30 million, with an average of eight people per square mile in Heilongjiang and 33 people per square mile in Jilin. The average for the three provinces (Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang) is only 28 people per square kilometer, which is far from the more than 142 people per square kilometer in the provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Guangdong. Although the climate of the three provinces is somewhat different from that of Beijing and Shanghai, it is definitely not as cold as people in the south generally say and imagine.

The Japanese say that the climate is not to be feared, and travelers also praise that the winters are not severely cold and the summers are not extremely hot, so the products are extremely abundant and suitable for farming and grazing. Agricultural products found in southern China, such as soybeans, sorghum, wheat, barley, dry grains, rice, corn, and white sesame, are all available in the Northeast. China's various seaports have a trade deficit, but only the Northeast has a trade surplus every year. The resources of the Northeast are not only the best in our country, but also among the best in the world. Taking the Northeast's mineral resources as an example, both metallic and non-metallic minerals are abundant, with high quality and beauty. The placer gold and gold nuggets in Heilongjiang are famous in the world and are coveted by the Russians. There are also mines producing iron, copper, lead, and other minerals, especially coal, with a very rich production volume of about 200 billion tons. The Fushun coal mine alone has more than 100 billion tons, which is a pity that the Japanese have been plundering and operating it, which is truly heartbreaking. If Japan's own coal production lasts for another 30 years, there will be no coal to meet its needs. Now that it has seized the Fushun coal mine, in addition to meeting its own needs, it also has a surplus to transport to Shanghai and other places. As for the forests of Jilin, which have been little cut down for thousands of years, the tall trees stretch across the mountains. Northerners have always called them a "sea of trees." The Japanese have long coveted the treasures of the Northeast in order to protect their own forests. The vast wilderness of Jilin and Heilongjiang is suitable for grazing. The number of livestock such as cattle, horses, sheep, mules, and camels is particularly large compared to those produced in other places, with an annual

birth rate of more than 15 million heads. The resources of the Northeast are so amazing just as mentioned above.

But it is only a rough and inadequate description, just to make southerners aware of the wealth and breadth of the Northeast. Last year, the sales of soybeans were sluggish and could not bear hoarding, and some people thought it was the end. But now the Japanese regard the Northeast as a major base for economic aggression. The South Manchuria Railway Company has a total investment of 600 million yuan in the Northeast provinces, with an annual business income of more than 240 million Japanese yen. It also researches and investigates various issues in the three provinces, writing special books with charts and explanations, never neglecting anything day and night. The Chinese people should understand the depth of their intentions. Mr. Tiecheng said, "If you don't go to the Northeast, you won't know the greatness of the Northeast; if you don't go to the Northeast, you won't know the crisis of the Northeast." Ambitious young people, entrepreneurs, and wealthy merchants in the country should immediately (go to the Northeast) conduct research and investigation, and develop it themselves. Mr. Ma Xiangbo said, "If you want to save China, first save the Northeast; if you want to save the Northeast, first govern the Northeast."

I would like to sincerely appeal to everyone present to quickly go to the Northeast. Now the government and people of the Northeast are working together to build the country, and transportation is becoming increasingly convenient. The railway network of the three provinces is now under construction. However, the Northeast is limited in talent, and it is hoped that talented people from all over the country will go to develop it and jointly save the Northeast. This is what the people of the Northeast desire most. Do not let the treasures given by Heaven be abandoned in the hands of foreigners and remain in a state of hesitation.

How can the Chinese people not wake up and embark on the path of self-salvation?

A total of one hundred and fifty-two boxes

Worth five million and one hundred thousand U.S. dollars, the North China Daily News says that the Central Bank, in order to facilitate the exchange market, has newly shipped one hundred and fifty-two boxes of gold bars to the United States on the Empress of Asia on Sunday afternoon for storage. Each box weighs one hundred and twenty-five pounds, with a total value of five million and one hundred thousand U.S. dollars. During the shipment, the Shanghai Municipal Council police and the

Huangpu River police provided protection along the way. It is reported that after these gold bars are shipped to the United States, they will still be the property of the Central Bank, but they will be deposited in New York as overseas gold reserves to facilitate the exchange market. If there is a need in the country,

they can still be shipped back at any time.

Pharmaceutical Industry Asks to Stop Shop Assistants from Organizing Unions 134

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a document to the Central Committee. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a document to the Central Committee yesterday, stating that it was submitting a report. On the 5th of this month, it received a letter from the Shanghai National Medicine Industry Association stating that the Chinese medicine industry in Shanghai has never had a trade union. Since the spring of the 16th year of the Republic of China, when the National Revolutionary Army settled in Southeast China, Communist Party members Zhou Xiang, Tao Wenbo, etc. were ordered by the Soviet Union to instigate shop assistants in the Shanghai medicine industry to organize a medicine and medicinal slice union with the goal of overthrowing capitalists. Therefore, immediately after its establishment, it gathered a crowd to destroy the Yi Hanchun Pharmacy in Xiaodongmen as a demonstration. Fortunately, the central government held a party purge and dissolved the Shanghai Federation of Trade Unions, and the medicine and medicinal slice union was also sealed off. When the Shanghai Trade Union Unification Committee was established, Tao Wenbo and others took the opportunity to call on medicine shop assistants to organize a medicine business union within the concession and continued to use their communist methods. They also destroyed the Liu Shouquan Pharmacy in Ximen and instructed the medicine masses to repeatedly strike to oppress the capitalists. The harm was unprecedented. Fortunately, the Shanghai Party and government organs were wise and decisive and ordered the medicine business union to be dissolved and reorganized into a medicine staff union. The communist atmosphere cleared, and their momentum was slightly frustrated. However, the Shanghai medicine shop assistants have been infected by the Communist Party for a long time, and their fierceness has increased. Last autumn, the industry staff union insisted on a strike for more than 40 days to force the capitalists to insert staff, and the losses of the city's medicine industry reached hundreds of thousands of gold. The case was serious and shocked the central government. It was not because the communist scourge had been severe for several years. This year, the central government's new trade union laws were promulgated and implemented, and the organization of staff unions is not applicable to the period of political tutelage. Shop assistants should join the industry and commerce trade association. The legislation is perfect, and the whole country is benefiting. The Shanghai medicine industry has suffered from disasters and is fortunate to bathe in the new law. The most fortunate thing is that the Central First 31st Standing Committee decided on the separate organization methods of medical and pharmaceutical groups, stipulating that medicine merchants and medicine staff should organize medicine trade associations in accordance with the industry and commerce trade association law, but workers in pharmaceutical factories may organize trade unions in accordance with the trade union law. The Shanghai medicine shops do not have pharmaceutical factories, so all shop assistants should join the association to be the right way. Unexpectedly, things are not so good. Now, the Shanghai medicine shop assistants have re-established a medicine trade union. At first, I did not know what basis it was based on. After several inquiries, I learned that the only reason for the shop assistants to organize the trade union was that the medicine shop assistants are all skilled workers and indirectly serve the shop, so they can organize a trade union, etc. According to the case, medicine shop assistants should learn all the internal and external affairs of the shop when they first enter the shop. This is a common sense that must be possessed for learning a profession. Not only the medicine industry is like this, but also the habits of other ordinary businesses are almost all like this. After the apprenticeship is over, the positions are assigned to the internal or external affairs according to their nature and ability. It is like the students of primary and secondary schools, who must take all the courses of the whole school. The situation is the same. If the medicine shop assistants have the common sense of this profession, they are said to have skills, then farmers who cultivate fields, merchants who buy and sell, soldiers who know the way of marching, and scholars who have the way of learning can all be said to have skills. Is there such a reason? The so-called indirect service is referred to the workers in the manufacturing factory who manufacture the goods and then have a distribution office set up by the factory to distribute them. The Shanghai medicine shops do not have pharmaceutical factories, and the shop assistants who serve in the shop on weekdays directly receive the customers, so how can they be indirectly serving? Now, a group of long-term unemployed medicine loafers want to maintain their personal lives and do not care about fabricating words and designing to forcibly organize trade unions, which involves destroying the spirit of national legislation and betraying the decision of the Central Committee. The association does not dare to be silent and especially presents the above warnings and humbly asks to forward them to the Central Committee to quickly dissolve the Shanghai Medicine Trade Union in accordance with the law and order the medicine shop assistants to join the association to comply with the law and eliminate disputes. It is a great benefit, etc. It was checked that the shop assistants illegally formed a trade union. The association requested the Ministry to handle it in accordance with the law on March 25th based on the request of the National Medicine Industry and 23 other trade associations. On April 16th, the Ministry issued an instruction No. 14597, stating that it is requested to prohibit the formation of another trade union in addition to participating in the trade association. According to the association's request, the Ministry has ordered the Shanghai Special Municipal Executive Committee's Public Training Committee to submit a detailed review for verification. It has not been reported yet. In addition to copying the original submission and ordering the committee to review the case together for verification, it is also notified to the association. Afterwards, how the verification is done has not been approved. However, the association received an instruction from the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau in another case stating that the Ministry of Industry has approved the Central Secretariat's letter sending the Shanghai Municipal Revised Trade Union Organization Plan, which has been approved by the Standing Committee and handled according to the plan. It is said that how the organization plan is drafted, how the workers are classified, all of this is related to the shop assistants joining the trade association. It is presumed that there is no conflict with the organization of the trade association without clear instructions. According to the association's strong statement of the abuses of the lack of standards for skilled workers, the association has added a detailed assessment and does not think it is unreasonable. All businesses have their business application knowledge and ability. Those who do not have this knowledge and ability are outsiders and not shop assistants. If those who have this knowledge and ability are skilled workers, then the name of shop assistants has long been nowhere to return. Why must there be a redundant provision in the same trade association law? The matter concerns national legislation and should not be suspected. It is reasonable to present the facts to the Ministry for review and humbly ask for the handling of the above two presentations (March 25th) in accordance with the law. It is a public convenience.

The longest discussion yesterday was on the issue of 2 million yuan for improved machinery, but no results were achieved at the end of the discussion. (2) Silk experts Zhou Junmei, Zheng Qunjiang, and Ge Jingzhong hope to use this opportunity to improve the long-strand silk industry machinery as a fundamental solution, so that it can compete with foreign silk in the future. And guarantee that there will be no more illegal detentions. The Shanghai Concession Taxpaying Chinese Association sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday, stating that according to the letter of Mr. Qiao Ru, today's newspaper carries a news item about the members of the Detective Police Protection Association detaining people. After reading it, I was both suspicious and fearful. I don't know who gave the Police Protection Association the power to detain people. A mere Portuguese Westerner claiming to be the director of the Police Protection Association can issue detention warrants and arbitrarily detain people, which is absurd. How will the Municipal Council explain itself? Your association is a representative organization of taxpayers. Two Assassinations Occur Near Shanghai West Zhongshan Road Overnight 145

Although Corpses Found in Two Locations

Investigation Suggests Same Incident

Yesterday morning around 1:00 AM, a major case occurred near Xujiazhai on the newly developed Zhongshan Road in Caojiadu, Shanghai West. Gunmen shot and killed two people. Although the bodies were found in two different locations, the investigation suggests that it was the same incident. The details are as follows:

Dog Barking Shatters Sweet Dreams - Farmer Hong Renzheng, a 44-year-old native of Tiantai, Zhejiang, lives at No. 26 Xujiazhai, near Zhongshan Road, Zhabei. He is a poor farmer with a wife, Chen, 36, and two young children. At around 1:00 AM yesterday, the entire family was fast asleep when they suddenly heard dogs barking loudly in the village. Hong was awakened from his dream, and the barking became louder and closer. Fearing that thieves were breaking in, Hong immediately got up and opened the door to investigate. As soon as he reached the door, four or five bandits suddenly emerged from the darkness, menacingly approaching him. At the same time, they drew their guns and threatened Hong.

Shouting "Thief" Leads to Gunfire - When Hong saw this, he knew he had encountered bandits. Although the bandits threatened him with their guns, Hong refused to be intimidated and shouted "Thief!" However, it was late at night, and the area was remote, so no one came to his aid. Seeing that the situation was not in their favor, the bandits shot at Hong several times. Hong's wife, Chen, initially saw her husband go out and then heard him shouting "Thief!" followed by several gunshots. She trembled in fear and dared not go out to investigate. When her husband did not return for a long time, she risked going outside, only to find Hong fatally wounded, lying in a pool of blood. The assailants had vanished without a trace. Overwhelmed with grief, she urgently called out to her neighbors and reported the incident to the Sixth District Police Station.

District Chief Investigates - Upon receiving the report, District Chief Ren, realizing the seriousness of the case, immediately led Inspector Xu, Detective Team Leader Liu Shaoqing, and other detectives to the scene. They found that Hong Renzheng's house had been ransacked and was very poor. The deceased had been shot in the right chest and left wrist, with blood flowing freely. One of the supporting posts of the clothing rack outside the house had been pulled out and discarded on the ground. A stone slab used to cover a ditch was also found in the yard, which was discovered to have been moved from a ditch about half a li from the house.

Another Body Discovered - While investigating, District Chief Ren and others came across another body about half a li from the house, near a small creek behind No. 23 Zhongshan Road. The body was of an unknown man, approximately thirty years old. Upon closer inspection, they found that the body was wearing old, torn blue cotton pants and had been shot in the left chest, with blood and flesh mangled. It was clear that he had also been shot. A small hat was found lying on the grass about ten feet from the body. Following the trail of blood on the road, they found that it led from Xujiazhai. Neighbors of Hong's house reported that they heard dogs barking loudly around midnight, and then again around 1:00 AM. Shortly after, they heard someone shouting "Thief!" followed by four or five gunshots. Knowing that it was gunfire, they did not dare to go out to investigate. Five six-inch pistol casings were collected from inside and outside Hong's house as evidence.

Speculation About the Two Murders - Based on the above information, it is speculated that the unknown man was an accomplice of the murderers. It is possible that the victim was killed in front of the Xu house due to some grudge, and the perpetrators moved the slab from a distant ditch to the site, intending to sink the body in the creek (since the body was missing its belt.) They were preparing to move the body to the creek but were interrupted by the dogs’ loud barking, preventing them from carrying out their plan. This could explain why the other victim was killed earlier around midnight, and the body was not moved. Later, around 1:00 AM, when Hong Renzheng heard the dogs barking and went outside to shout, he was shot. Seeing that no one was coming out, the perpetrators used the wooden post from the clothing rack as a lever to carry the unidentified body to the creek, making it difficult to trace. Otherwise, if they were robbing the Hong's house, they wouldn’t have killed them since there wasn’t much of value there. In any case, the truth remains to be determined.

Court Sends Officials to Investigate - After conducting the initial investigation, District Chief Ren ordered Detective Team Leader Liu Shaoqing to urgently investigate the perpetrators. He also instructed Wang Zhangkun, the head of the 11th Tu, and Zhang Zitang, the head of the 10th Tu, to report to the local court. Around 3:20 PM, the court dispatched Prosecutor Yang Wenjun and Clerk Mao Zhenxin, along with a coroner, to the scene to conduct an investigation.

They confirmed that both men had been fatally shot before their deaths. The body of Hong Renzheng was claimed by his wife, Chen, for burial. The body of the unknown man was reported to the local authorities for burial.

Suicide of Jida Staff Member Zhu Peigen 146

Once Said Suicide is Best Done by Hanging

The Ominous Remarks Became Reality

Zhu Peigen, a staff member of the Nanyang Cultural Department of Jida University, committed suicide in his dormitory yesterday morning. The faculty and students of the entire university were shocked by the news. The deceased was 40 years old, a native of Jiading, known for his calligraphy. He was diligent and disciplined in his work. The reason for his suicide is unknown.

Hanging by the Window - Zhu Peigen had been serving as a staff member and assistant in the Nanyang Cultural Department of Jida University for three years. He was recommended to the school by the China Vocational Education Society. He was known for his punctuality and had good relationships with his colleagues. He lived in dormitory number 19, sharing a room with Mr. Yao. The previous night, Mr. Yao went to Shanghai, leaving Zhu alone in the room. Yesterday morning, Zhu had not gotten up for a long time. The tea boy peeked through the window and saw Zhu hanging by a rope from the window.

Cause of Death Unknown - The deceased was a man of few words, rarely smiling or interacting with others. His family and friends searched his room but found no suicide note. There had been no significant changes in his behavior recently. However, it was said that after a teacher named Zhao from the affiliated elementary school committed suicide due to a broken heart, Zhu had discussed it with others, saying that hanging was the best way to commit suicide. Who knew that his remarks would become an ominous prediction? Zhu's elderly mother lives in Jiading. He is survived by four children and two brothers who are self-sufficient. Zhu earned about 60 yuan a month at the school, which was enough to support himself. His body was placed in a coffin last night and will be transported back to his hometown today.

Gospel for Sojourning Patients in Shanghai (By Chen Jingkang of Beiping) 150

Now is the time when summer decrees and diseases flourish. Even a slight mishap can lead to illness. People fear disease more than any ferocious beast. This is especially true for those who are living alone in Shanghai. Once they fall ill, finding a doctor is difficult, and taking medicine is even more inconvenient. Lying in bed with an illness, one must ask others to help prepare and decoct the medicine. However, those who help often lack experience in decocting medicine, resulting in a heavy price with little effect. I am one of those living in Shanghai who has fallen ill and knows the difficulties involved. A few days ago, I came to Shanghai and stayed at the New World Hotel. I fell ill because I was unable to find the friend I was trying to visit. Although I had a tea boy serving me in Shanghai, it was not as attentive as my parents or wife. I wanted to prescribe and decoct the medicine myself, but I had concerns. Although I took several doses of medicine, they were not effective. At this time, I was suffering from the inconvenience of taking and decocting medicine. Fortunately, I read an advertisement for Wang Yuandao Chinese Medicine Store in the newspaper. The store had departments for receiving prescriptions, delivering medicine, and decocting medicine for customers. I was overjoyed to learn of this convenience. I immediately called the store to pick up the prescription. Soon, a messenger in yellow arrived by scooter. I handed him the prescription and entrusted him with the decoction. After a while, the messenger returned with two thermos bottles, one containing the first decoction and the other containing the second decoction. Another box contained the squeezed medicine residue. He asked me to check each item to ensure it matched the medicine listed on the prescription. Although I had no in-depth experience in identifying medicines, I knew a thing or two. The medicine was authentic, and the decoction was strong and thick. I was able to take the medicine with peace of mind. After several days, my illness vanished. I believe that this service provided by the store is of great benefit to patients. I hope that those who sympathize with my situation will try it. The store is located at the Jiaqiao in the French Concession. The telephone number is 1315. Room number 12. The team leader of the police squad, Dai Shouquan, came to Shen to apply to the Lao Zha police station on the day before yesterday. If a detective named Huang Yinjie is sent secretly to take Xue and bring him to the Special Zone Local court, it will be handled by Judge Xu in court.

A Woman Married Twice 151

Ru Longsheng Loses Both Money and People

Zhang Hengyao Commits Fraud

Ru Longsheng, 27 years old, a native of Suzhou, currently lives at No. 409 Fujian Road and works at Dr. Cai's clinic. Although his income is not high, he lives frugally and has saved some money. Last year, his mother saw that he was getting older and wanted to find him a wife.

She spoke to Zhu Bingquan, the owner of Zhutai Clothing Store at No. 1911 Hele Lane, Xin Zha Road, about this matter. Zhu had a friend named Wu Dayi, who knew Zhang Hengyao, a native of Zhenjiang, who said he had a daughter who was of marriageable age. Zhu and Wu acted as matchmakers and arranged the marriage. However, after living together for several months, the Zhenjiang Court informed the Shanghai Special District Court that his wife was already married. The court summoned his wife, and Ru Longsheng lost both his money and his wife. He filed a complaint with the Special District Court, requesting that the defendants be punished and seeking incidental civil compensation. His complaint stated that the defendants falsely presented a married woman as a virgin and fraudulently married her to him. Zhang Hengyao, Wu Dayi, and Zhu Bingquan claimed in April of last year that Zhang Hengyao's daughter was 22 years old and still unmarried. They acted as matchmakers and demanded a betrothal gift of 186 yuan, as well as clothes and jewelry. The wedding was held at the Tongyu Hotel on May 26. After the marriage, it was discovered that she was not a virgin. To protect his reputation, he did not make an issue of it. However, on November 4, the court police arrested his wife and informed him that she was already married to a man named Xu and was not named Zhang but Xiao. Zhang Hengyao was her stepfather. Her aunt had accused her of bigamy in the Zhenjiang Court, so the case was brought to trial. Only then did he realize he had been deceived. He engaged a lawyer to negotiate with them, but the defendants refused to admit the truth. Therefore, they are undoubtedly guilty of fraud and should be punished. He is requesting compensation for 449 yuan, etc.

Yesterday, Judge Wu Tingqi presided over the hearing in the Second Criminal Court. The plaintiff testified as described above and requested compensation for 449 yuan. When questioned, Zhu Bingquan admitted to being a matchmaker but claimed that he did not know she was married and did not handle the betrothal gifts. He said he gave it all to the female matchmaker, Wu Dayi. Wu Dayi testified that he also gave all the betrothal gifts to Zhang Hengyao and did not take any money. Zhang Hengyao also testified that he married his stepdaughter to Ru Longsheng but stated that he had declared that the girl was remarrying because she had disagreements with her family. He only received 120 yuan in betrothal gifts. Judge Wu reviewed the testimony and announced in court that Zhang Hengyao was guilty of fraud and sentenced to two years imprisonment. This sentence will be combined with the three-and-a-half-year sentence for inciting bigamy that was confirmed by the Zhenjiang Court, resulting in a total sentence of three years and six months. Zhu Bingquan and Wu Dayi were found not guilty. The civil compensation portion of the case was transferred to the Civil Court for trial.

An Unlikely Fortune for a Water Carrier 152

Gold and Silver Ornaments Discovered by the Riverbank

Zhang Asan, a water carrier from a tofu shop in the Pingyuan Alley, Doushi Road, Wusong, aged thirty-eight, was carrying water buckets around 3 PM yesterday afternoon. He was at the Guangbian area in front of the Tongxing Wharf on the outer side of the road, drawing water. Unintentionally, his foot touched something in the muddy bottom of the water. He felt something pulling at him and was quite curious. So, he stopped at a nearby ferry and borrowed a bamboo pole to scoop the object from the water. Unexpectedly, upon closer inspection, the item retrieved turned out to be gold and silver bracelets, chains, and other ornaments, totaling about seventeen or eighteen pieces linked together in a large string. However, because these bracelets and chains had been submerged in water for a long time, their color was not very bright. Zhang initially suspected they were copper and not valuable. Later, after being identified by bystanders, he realized they were all genuine articles estimated to be worth three to four hundred gold coins. Zhang was overjoyed. He gave one gold and one silver bracelet to the people on the ferry as a reward for borrowing the pole. He took the rest home, causing a great stir and becoming a local legend.

Conclusion of the Case of the Chung Ngoi Pharmacy Confiscating a Large Quantity of Poisonous Substances 153

The Verdict Is Scheduled to Be Announced Tomorrow Morning

The Chung Ngoi Pharmacy on Guangdong Road was found by the Public Concession Police to be selling illegal items. They petitioned the Special District Court for a search warrant, and detectives were dispatched to the pharmacy. They confiscated 434 taels, 3 maces, and 4 fen of morphine; 13 taels of aconite; 473 taels of opium; 816 taels of "ka fen" (likely a type of medicinal powder); 304 taels of red pill material; 78 and a half taels of red pill fragrance; over 160 red pills; three cans of opium paste; two opium pipes; one fountain pen-style poisonous gas pistol; five bullets; over two thousand yuan in silver dollars, gold pounds, and banknotes; one hundred and thirty yuan in Tianjin banknotes; sixty yuan in counterfeit banknotes; two hundred and fifty-six counterfeit double dime coins. They also detained manager Su Renjie, accountant Wang Ruilai, Qiao Zihang, the owner of Wanfeng Lumber in Pudong, Zhu Gao (also known as Qu Gao), a clerk at the Meifeng Bank, Sun Chunsheng, a broker at the Yarn Exchange, and ten other employees, including Qian Genmei, Qiu Ada, Cao Chengen, Zhang Shiqi, and Du Shutian. It was also discovered that Qiao Zihang had also sold morphine in 1922 and was punished with six months of imprisonment, handed over to the Special District Court for interrogation. Judge Xu Jiashi, the presiding judge of the criminal division, personally inspected the pharmacy. The court session resumed yesterday morning. The police lawyer stated that Huang Yicai, the manager of the Meifeng Bank, whom the court intended to summon as a witness, had already been questioned. Huang Yicai testified that the defendant, Zhu Gao, was indeed a clerk in his bank and had been there for four years. He was usually quite cautious. His guarantor was the Chung Ngoi Pharmacy. He also lived in the pharmacy because his relatives worked there. When asked by the court if he was a shareholder of the pharmacy, he said he had heard He Ruiren say so, but he could not confirm it. Wang Ruilai testified that he was the external accountant and that the morphine matter was handled by the internal accountant and he did not interfere or know about it. Su Renjie testified that he was a junior employee of the Chung Ngoi Pharmacy and not the manager, and he knew nothing about the morphine. The defendant's lawyer, Jiang Yiping, then presented a letter from the Qingdong District Party Headquarters proving that Qiao Zihang was indeed the legitimate owner of a lumber business in Pudong and had a proper reputation. He then submitted it to the court for examination. The court asked the defendant, Shen Chunsheng, if he was a broker at the Yarn Exchange, but the court's inquiry stated that the exchange had no broker named Shen Chunsheng. Shen replied that he handled cash transactions. Judge Xu then ordered Shen to write numbers to compare his handwriting with the writing in the Chung Ngoi Pharmacy's books. After Shen finished writing, the police lawyer and the defendant's lawyer began to debate at length. Judge Xu then announced that the debate in the case was concluded and that the verdict would be announced tomorrow (Wednesday) morning.

The Easy-to-Check Telegraph Code Book Is Published 164

The Easy-to-Check Telegraph Code Book compiled by Mr. Xiao Guohua is extremely convenient for the application of telegraphs. The book is divided into three parts: (1) the New Telegraph Code Book, which lists the radicals in rows and columns and is attached with the Roman characters of the code, so that users can know it at a glance and can send telegrams according to foreign telegram examples; (2) the Telegraph Homophone Lexicon, which compiles the words in the New Telegraph Code Book according to the national pronunciation, so that those who are familiar with the national pronunciation or Roman spelling can find words according to the pronunciation, which is convenient for checking and translating; (3) the Code of Substituted Words, which is divided into traveler's terms, family terms, merchant's terms, general terms, etc., so that a few words can express tens of words. Using this book for telegraphs is both easy for translation and saves a lot of money. The book has been published and entrusted to the Renji Kou Road Branch at 141 Sichuan Road in this city as the general distributor.

A Grand Opening of the National Goods Market 168

— Sun Choucheng

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Commodity Exhibition Hall has been operating for ten years. Recently, foreign goods have been repelling domestic goods in the market. Therefore, those who love to use domestic goods have nowhere to buy them. Therefore, a National Goods Market has been specially set up to gather the essence of domestic products for the selection of Chinese people. The opening ceremony was held on the station day of this month. The general situation has been recorded in this newspaper. Regarding the promotion of national goods, I will record the trivial matters seen and heard on that day and send them to this talk for readers to enjoy.

On that day, the party and national flags were crossed at the entrance of the Chamber of Commerce, with a bamboo cloth banner hanging in the middle that read "Opening Ceremony of the National Goods Market of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Commodity Exhibition Hall". Armed guards and patrolmen were stationed on both sides, and posters were posted all over the walls on both sides of the aisle (Promote National Goods Starting from the National Goods Market) (Using National Goods Is the People's Natural Duty). They were all written on red and green Chinese paper. The auditorium was in the main conference hall, and a registration desk was set up at the entrance. After signing in, guests were given a bag of domestic goods containing cigarettes, toothpaste, monosodium glutamate, Rendan, Zhongshan olives, etc., so they all smiled happily. At 9:00, after playing military music, Wang Xiaolai and Ye Huijun both wore red silk chairman symbols and led representatives of various organizations to the stage. If this continues, the outflow of rights and interests will be unbearable. In view of this, our association has specially set up a National Goods Market so that patriotic compatriots will not be dazzled and unable to distinguish when they want to buy national goods. After the description, he said that this was the opening speech, and then he took out a report form from his chest, held it in both hands, and read it aloud in public, just like the Taoist priest's general statement during the Buddhist monk's practice, which made everyone laugh. The representative of the municipal government gave a speech, saying that our country is vast, has abundant resources, and a large population, but it cannot be self-reliant because the general merchants do not have a global perspective and sell foreign goods for profit. Consumers do not know what are domestic goods and what are foreign goods when they enter the market. They only choose beautiful and cheap ones to buy and use. Now that domestic goods are gathered in one place, so that people can recognize domestic goods, those who have a little conscience will definitely not buy foreign goods again. Dong Kerren, the representative of the Social Affairs Bureau, said that in addition to detailing the past experiences of the Shanghai National Goods Exhibition Hall, he was also afraid of causing criticism because he was wearing a suit, so he declared in public that this was a domestic suit. If you don't believe me, you can try the fabric today in the National Goods Market for sale. Wang Jie'an, the representative of the Suzhou Chamber of Commerce, gave a speech detailing how foreigners sell raw materials from our country at low prices and then, in a change of hand, still sell the finished products to our country. The weakness of the country and the poverty of the people for decades are all due to this. I hope that compatriots will wake up. After Xiao Jinqing, the deputy minister of the Ministry of Industry, arrived late, he immediately handed the congratulatory speech given by Minister Kong Xiangxi to Wang Xiaolai. It was a horizontal plaque of gold-splashed paper on white background with more than twenty four-character titles. After Mr. Wang accepted it, he handed it to the master of ceremonies, Xue Guangqian, to post it in front of the stage, together with the vertical axes sent by Lu Xingzhuang and others from the Shanghai National Goods Factory Joint Association (Promote the National Glory) (Save the Rights and Interests). After Wang Liwu distributed the National Goods Introduction Compilation edited by him on the spot, Wang Xiaolai led all the guests to visit the National Goods Market. Limited by the location, only one company in each industry is allowed to participate, and no similar ones are allowed to mix in. All the kitchen cabinets are uniform and very tidy. The cosmetics sold in the Huahua store are categorized and fragrant, and everyone stopped to buy them in crowds. I returned to the inkstone to write this at eleven o'clock.

Common Sense About Drinking 169

— Jian Fu

American newspapers recently reported that about a quarter of Chinese people die from alcohol. In view of this, the government has issued an order to ban it. Commentators say that the American alcohol prohibition is comparable to our country's opium prohibition. I say that we should regard alcohol and tobacco as poisons and fear them like snakes. Then there will be no harm to life. In ancient China, it was often said that alcohol was used to complete etiquette, and it became a custom. Therefore, some people were morally corrupt, but there were not many who died from alcohol. When Da Yu hated sweet wine, it was because he was afraid that the ruler would neglect government affairs. Confucius's unwillingness to be troubled by wine was to encourage scholars not to waste their studies. The rest, such as Zhaolie's prohibition of brewing to maintain the people's food, and Ji Ruan's indulgence in drinking to dispel the worries of the world, are not related to this article, so I will not discuss them here.

As for alcohol, although it is a harmful product, the problem is that we do not exercise self-restraint. However, after examining the reasons for not exercising self-restraint, it is only because we drink alcohol together and actually do not have common sense about drinking. In modern times, science is prosperous, and it is said that drinking too much alcohol can harm sperm and hinder fertility. I did not deeply believe this at first. A certain member of my clan was indeed fond of drinking, and had more than five children who all died young. So he resolutely quit drinking and then had a son who is now five years old. Then I realized that the reason why the previous children did not live long was because they were harmed by alcohol. So the theory that sperm is harmed is not entirely unfounded.

Drinking a little alcohol can activate blood circulation and help digestion, which is beneficial to physical health. It is forbidden to sleep after drinking, as sleeping will stop digestion. It is also forbidden to engage in sexual intercourse, as engaging in sexual intercourse will reverse the five internal organs. This is what researchers of hygiene should pay the most attention to. Other things, such as drinking quickly for a long time, can cause dry heaving, and drinking hot drinks is most likely to harm the lungs. Although we know this well, we often do not pay attention. Also, drinking cold alcohol will produce alcohol mold, although this is unfounded, there is also a true principle. Microbes often grow in alcohol, which is a type of parasite, like vinegar eels in vinegar, and cannot be distinguished by the naked eye, so it is easy to overlook. Only warming the alcohol to a warm temperature before drinking can eliminate this harm.

Talking About Fishing Boats Today 170

— Ge Yaocheng, sent from Hangzhou

The flowers have fallen in Jiangnan, and it is once again the end of spring. On the banks of the Quanzhou River, where the flowers are in decline, there is once again news of the inspection of prostitutes in the south. Because of this, I recall the old story of the Nine Surname Fishing Boats and record it in Free Talk for the purpose of aiding conversation.

When Emperor Taizu of Ming set Jinling, it was rumored that the Nine Surname Fishing Boats were all the tribes of Zhang Shicheng. When Zhang Shicheng's army was defeated, Emperor Taizu banished them to low-level industries, using boats as homes and not allowing them to land. Although they were called fishing boats, they actually relied on selling laughter for income. They were mostly moored on the Jianggan River. People in Hangzhou named them Jiangshan Boats. The name Jiangshan County may have originated from this, so it was named that. But the common name is Jiang Bai Boats, so it is not known where it came from. Those who are married are called "Fellow-Year Sisters-in-Law," and those who are not married are called "Fellow-Year Sisters." The so-called "Nine Family Sisters Two Fellow-Years" is also true, but according to both versions of the Autumn Rain Collection, "Fellow-Year" is actually a homonym of "Tongyan." At that time, there was Bao Zhupo, the vice minister, who was confused by the boat prostitutes and dismissed from his post. There was also a member of the imperial family, an Eight Banner celebrity, who wrote the phrase "Grass Jiangshan Nine Surname Beauty Hemp." Going up the river, Fuchun, Xindeng, Tonglu, and Yanzhou were all places where officials and merchants spent money to buy boats for travel. When the ministers were melancholy, the prostitutes would accompany the guests and offer wine. When the river moon first rose, the tide was calm, and the banks were full of boats, carrying the Tanlang away. At that time, the nightingales and swallows were reflected in the moonlight, the fragrant mouths were slightly opened, and the Tanboard was lightly slapped. The gentlemen were surrounded by the wine bottles. The brocade curtains were warm in the rear cabin, and the mandarin duck pillows were in pairs. It was a place where clay figurines lost their souls. After the change of dynasty, the fellow-year sisters successively left the boat and landed on the shore, settling in the neighborhood of the Haiyue Bridge and Huapai Building, which had already lost the meaning of the Jiangshan Boats. Last year, the lottery ordered the abolition of prostitution, and the enthusiasm was low. Now, the Hangzhou Municipal Government, together with the Provincial Public Security Bureau, has issued an order to inspect prostitutes. The inspection in the north has just been completed, and the inspection in the south is about to begin. At that time, the nightingales and swallows were terrified, claiming that their dignity was at stake. Therefore, they were led by Qian and others and submitted their cases to the authorities, requesting exemption from inspection.

Correction

Yesterday (Tan Dong’s Crude Customs), the title was missing (Wang Yanjin) three words, and the (4) under the title Lakeside Anecdotes was a mistake for “6”. We specifically correct it here.

Record of "Longevity Mother's Painting at Lan Terrace" 171

— Old Man Sanyuan

Jiangning's Jiang Guobang, styled Suchang, is a gentle and refined scholar, diligent in his studies and skilled in writing. He is especially known for his filial piety towards his widowed mother, Madam Ma. I have known Suchang for twenty years and am pleased to see his scholarship progressing, his conduct becoming more cautious, his heart more humble, and his temperament becoming more calm. It is indeed true that an orphaned son has been raised by his mother's teachings, a fact that is widely acknowledged among the literati and officials. In the fourth month of the year Xinwei, Madam Ma celebrated her seventieth birthday. Suchang requested Mr. Xiao Wuquan to paint "Longevity Mother's Painting at Lan Terrace" and sent it to me in the mountains of Kuanglu, asking me to write a record for it. Suchang said, "My mother, Madam Ma, is from a family in Shu. Her father, who served as the prefect of Zhangzhou, was my maternal grandfather, Zhen. From a young age, she was composed and well-versed in etiquette. She studied alongside her uncles and became proficient in literature and history. At the age of twenty, she married my father, Houmin, the prefect. She was obedient to her parents-in-law, harmonious with her sisters-in-law, and affectionate towards the servants. Although my father lived in luxury, he was diligent and frugal as if he were poor. He often studied at the Xiaosi Temple in the south of the city. My mother carefully prepared his meals and clothing, and occasionally discussed literature with him. My father's scholarship improved daily. When my father became seriously ill, my mother cut her arm to mix blood with the medicine several times, but he eventually passed away, leaving behind two orphaned sons: Guobang, who was four years old, and his younger brother, Guoping, who was three years old. My mother endured her sorrow and suffering and from then on, she never wore elaborate clothing. She raised Guobang and his brother without relying on wet nurses. When they were old enough to attend school, she urged them to get up at dawn and stayed up late to read with them, making sure they memorized the day's lessons before allowing them to rest. If they did not meet her expectations or committed other mistakes, she would scold them severely without any leniency. My mother was both a loving mother and a strict teacher. Furthermore, my father enjoyed giving generously, and my mother supported him wholeheartedly. Since then, she has provided relief to disaster-stricken provinces, established charity granaries in Jinling, and assisted the poor, amounting to millions of dollars. In the third year of Xuantong, the village elders requested the court to commend her for her chastity and filial piety, and built an archway as well as a 'Good Deeds and Charitable Giving' memorial. Guobang wrote a postscript, which was engraved on stone. Contemporary teachers and scholars also wrote articles praising her. Thus, my mother's virtuous conduct and exemplary character became widely known. When the Wuchang Uprising occurred in the year Xinhai, Jinling was also in chaos. Our family hastily fled to Shanghai. Unfortunately, my younger brother, Guotian, passed away prematurely. My mother was overwhelmed with grief. Guobang then purchased a modestly priced residence by the South Lake in Hangzhou and renovated it, naming the bridges and pavilions 'Lan Terrace Villa' in the hope of entertaining my mother and alleviating her sorrow. Later, my wife, née Chou, also passed away from illness. Fortunately, Guobang remarried to Madam Feng, who is able to fulfill her duties as a wife, and is also knowledgeable in literature and skilled in painting. Furthermore, my two grandsons recite the classics and seem to have some understanding of them. This brings some joy to my mother. However, Guobang is mediocre. Although he owes his success to my mother, he has not been abandoned by renowned scholars and elders. Despite encountering world changes, he has no intention of pursuing advancement and bringing honor to my mother. How can he not feel ashamed?" In summary, according to Suchang's account, Madam Ma's fortitude, perseverance, pure and single-minded conduct, and sincere and deep affection are in line with the virtuous mothers recorded in history. She has rightfully raised a virtuous son who repays her kindness. This is also a natural result. It is important to remember that the greatest form of filial piety is nurturing one's ambition, and the greatest way to nurture one's ambition is through self-cultivation and diligent study. Relying on power, influence, and wealth for fame and glory is not the way. Moreover, we are living in an era of unprecedented change, where moral principles have collapsed and reckless behavior is rampant. Is this not a time when Heaven closes and virtuous people hide? If one still harbors thoughts of fame and fortune or blindly adheres to the notion that every patriotic commoner has a responsibility, and rashly attempts to change things, one will only disgrace oneself and one's parents, which is not in line with nurturing one's ambition. Suchang's discernment is evident. Therefore, Lan Terrace Villa is Suchang's earnest attempt to purchase a place for his mother to live in seclusion without complaint, so that he can nurture her ambition. The location boasts the beauty of the inner lake. The Nine Luminaries, Jade Emperor, Three Terraces, and other peaks rise and surround the area. The shimmering waves and mountain scenery create a captivating spectacle, with clouds, flowers, trees, fish, and birds offering a unique and ever-changing view. Suchang respectfully provides Madam Ma with a comfortable retreat, allowing her to immerse herself in the pure and beautiful atmosphere of the lake and mountains. Suchang also enriches the environment with his literary talents, guiding the women and children with kindness, creating a harmonious blend of natural and human sounds that soothe Madam Ma's decades of hardship and usher in auspicious blessings. It is as if the beautiful and ethereal capital is still present in the human world. Heaven is kind to Madam Ma and encourages Suchang to strive for constant and uninterrupted improvement. All of this lies within this painting, which is a symbol of auspicious response.

The Storytelling Society

Random Musings on the Lake (7) 172

— Tianxu Wosheng

Wild tea is found only in deep mountain ravines. Those who risk their lives to obtain it do so as quickly as possible. Therefore, they do not wait for it to fully mature but harvest it as soon as possible. They also do not know how to properly roast and bake it. They simply stir and twist it into a bead-like shape in a pot. The shape is very unattractive, curled and thin, resembling lotus seeds. The price is extremely high, always three or four yuan per tael, and it is very rare. One can accumulate less than a pound in a spring. Those who do not know tea are unwilling to buy it, so only tea professionals highly value it (wild mountain tea) as the best of the best. The "Compendium of Materia Medica" states that tea picked before the rain must be aged for three years before drinking to remove its fire toxins. Li Shizhen also spoke extensively about the harmful effects of tea on people. According to my observations, people in Hangzhou drink tea in small amounts as a form of leisurely enjoyment, not as an addiction, like those who indulge in alcohol. Wealthy families buy new tea from mountain villages as soon as it comes on the market, mostly from those who tend their ancestral graves. The amount they purchase is enough to last a year, and they store it for three years before drinking it. They do not use it in the same year. This is similar to newly brewed wine, which must be stored for three years. However, only wealthy families can afford to prepare in advance with such leisure. Therefore, there is no three-year aged tea available in the market, just like three-year aged wine. Wines that are called "aged" are simply those that have been brewed with an extra process the previous year. For example, if six dou of rice were originally used, eight dou are now used to reduce the water content, so it is called extra brewing. There is also so-called home-brewed wine, which is brewed by families for their own consumption and to entertain guests. Its age can often be determined. For example, when a son or daughter is born, wine is brewed and stored, and its name is used as a marker. There is so-called "newborn wine" or "daughter wine." When the daughter marries, it is decorated with painted carvings, often with raised patterns such as melon ribs or round dots, with auspicious words written inside for the third-day celebration. It is called "painted carving." When a son achieves success in the imperial examinations, it is used to treat guests and is called "Scholar Red." Its age is the same as the person's age. If he does not pass the examinations in his lifetime, it is used to celebrate his sixtieth birthday. If the family does not fall on hard times, it will never be sold to others. Therefore, the wines sold on the market are merely imitations. The common wine with a light color and weak taste is called "Filial Piety and Chastity," which refers to the wine brewed when a woman is engaged but her husband dies before marriage, and she remains chaste like Bei Gong Yinger. Because the wine brewed at the time of her birth is useless, she opens it on her parents' birthdays to honor them. Therefore, it is called "Filial Piety and Chastity." Its age is not old, and its color is clear and thin, like bamboo leaf soup, so it is also called "Bamboo Leaf Green." As for the white wine called "Traveler," it is specifically supplied to wine merchants for wholesale. Therefore, its value is the lowest. In the secret language of the manufacturers, it is said that this is not for retail but for wholesale. Only four dou of rice are used for one shi of wine. The wine sold retail in Hangzhou is generally called Shaoxing, which is the "Traveler" wine with water added. The wine called "Aged" is simply "Traveler" wine with caramel color and water added. Only the "Painted Carving" wine is not adulterated, but it is all brewed in the winter of the previous year. Unless you buy it yourself, it is like seeking three-year aged moxa for a seven-year illness in the market; you will never find it in a pharmacy. (The End)

Silk and Tea: Wuxi's Superior Cocoons Arrive, Scarce and Expensive 180

Each village is asking for 80 yuan, and each trade is raising prices to compete for purchases. Wuxi's four rural cocoon markets have opened a total of 136 shops. Weighing has been underway for four or five days. This year's cocoon production is exceptionally poor, with the total yield only about a third of normal years. Each trade's purchase volume is insufficient, only forty or fifty loads per day, at most just over a hundred. Goods arriving on the market are not flowing smoothly, and superior cocoons are especially scarce. In places like Yuqi, Luoshe, Yangshu, Yuansi, Toushiqiao, and Bashiqiao, because each trade is raising prices to compete for purchases, the highest price for superior cocoons has reached above 80 yuan, and even ordinary ones require around 60 yuan.
